#  [](/thread/86476-5-min-keltner-system)5 Min Keltner System 

  * 

  * [#361](/thread/post/2067566#post2067566 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 21, 2008 5:20am  Jun 21, 2008 5:20am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar56490_3.gif) Paulus](paulus)

  * Joined Dec 2007 | Status: Trader | [2,600 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56490)

Funny movement in the mkt today nice moves but few signals..  
  
here are the signals for 5min confirmed by 15min as outlined in my last couple posts.  
  
If using the 15 min stoch to close..ie when we go short on the 5min and the 15 min stoch is also over bought we close using the stoch on the 15min time frame when it reaches over sold we close...  
  
But  
  
What happens if it doesnt get to over sold and just reverses before geting below 20..easy one this when you go short on the 5min bring your trade to break even when we hit the bottom keltner line on the 5min..if we reverse on the 15min now we are at break even..we only want the best signals getting through using this 5/15 stoch combination.  
  
Result +9 +9 +0 +0 +0 +31 +0 = +41   
  
here are today signals.. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

> Ignored

I think the answer to your question is the 2 pip spread. The stop should be 1 + spread (so price actually gets 1 pip below before you are stoped out). Or one other possibility is that I put in a variable for the minimum stop loss, so if the entry price is too close the the high,low of the signal bar, it with use a set stop loss. That is because some brokers have a minimum stop loss they will let you use. If you put in one too close, you will get an error for your order.  
  
Also, the price never got to the limit price until that down bar, it retraced 1 pip, but not two (at least that is what it looks like to me, and my best guess as to why that is when it entered).

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar60923_5.gif) Juan Grande](juan*grande)

  * | Joined Feb 2008  | Status: Knowledge is good | [117 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=60923)

I just finished the thread as well. Two days, with all the charts to look at. Many thanks go to Paulus for all the efforts to date. It takes quite a committment of time to make all those posts, charts and replies. Hope all is well with you and yours.  
  
Also Jacioux helped crystalize a nebulous idea that was already floating around in my head as I was reading -- use of an IB candle instead of the RSI technique as a possible trend reversal signal. Ta mate. I already employ an IB setup on the 15M, and will try to marry these two by putting the 5 and 15 side by side. Slightly diff stoch settings, but we'll see. At the very minimum, it would seem to be an excellent entry confirmation to add to the warchest.  
  
Also I would second Peej's remarks on S/R (Hoss made reference too). PJ, your charts were well-presented. I appreciate the overall scalping aspect, but also believe its a good idea to at least be aware of the major S/R levels on the longer term charts. Which, on this time frame, IMHO, would generally be 15, 60 and 240. Put em on the same chart. Maybe start with the 240, mark em. Then change timeframe to 60 and repeat. Keep bringing them forward til you get to the 5m. Save to chart. And there they are, along with the 00's and 50's, waiting for price. Doesnt take that long and is worth it. If they bug you (I admit they bug me sometimes), fade them into the background color. Trend lines, trend channels, horizontal lines, fibs, pivots, whatever your pleasure. I am pretty sure biggie big bank is aware of them. I hope that is not speaking out of school.  
  
Thanks again to all involved.

  * [#391](/thread/post/2089069#post2089069 "Post Permalink")

  * Jul 3, 2008 12:55pm  Jul 3, 2008 12:55pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar60923_5.gif) Juan Grande](juan*grande)

  * | Joined Feb 2008  | Status: Knowledge is good | [117 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=60923)

Followup from message above regarding attempt to incorporate this method into 15M chart with IB/OB entry. Note times are EDT. Note also, my stoch setting is slightly different.  
  
First chart is EUR. Upon London open, price breaks above Asian high, then has a green candle close outside the K. Next bar is red, but I am waiting on an IB/OB which forms as the next candle (circled), but wrong color for Paulus' method. This is my signal so I establish entry price at low of IB, which hits the next candle. Stochs and ADX favorable, and you can also see SMA crossover. The clincher was the significant stoch divergence. Stop set at high of bar preceding IB (fucia lines).   
  
After enduring fairly long inverted hammer, take 1/2 at the 00 (which I verbal as the "uh-oo"). Move stop down. I had a TP below where it bottomed, so manually closed at the next IB marked by the arrow. That exit bar is also a Paulus setup with close below the K. And it would have worked had you set your stop at the low of the bar preceding the IB. I did not take that one but did take the one circled, occuring as NY got to work, but not a Paulus trade so wont discuss (in hindsight, i was too eager with this second entry. it worked, but still....)  
  
The second chart is the GBP from the same time period (these are the two pairs I watch). The signal candle here was an OB that formed after a K setup (circled). Entry was not until two candles later, long red one. Stop set at high of the OB (see fucia lines). Stochs, ADX and SMAs all confirmed + stoch divergence.   
  
Closed 1/2 at the 00s, and moved stop down on other half. Note the inverted (green) hammer around that time -- Paulus' RSI filter warned you off that as a possible entry (lower low). My target was 9840 based on S/R to the left but it did not hit so manually closed at next IB marked by arrow. Next entry (long) is shown too but did not fit the entry parameters here to warrant discussion.  
  
Anyway, this is a different style, not 5M scalping. But does tend to show, at least for today and these two pairs, Paulus' method has validity on a longer term chart as well. Both on entry, and use of the RSI to keep you out of a bad countertrend signal.  
  
So thanks again to Paulus for bringing this style over. By coincidence, I attended Traders Int'l as well around that same time. If you took the class in Austin, who knows, we may have been sitting beside one another! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

I have incorporated this system along 15min TF too plus other TFs, I have added CCI woodies and MACD, and look at the daily rythm indicated by CCI on 5 min and 15 min TF. I also use Delta with EW and Fibs, and try to trade only in the direction of Delta. I mostly trade G/U pair. I try not to take profits less then 20 pps, and allow the trade to run, in the direction of delta, monitorred on 5min, 15min, 1hr and 4hr TF. It was a challenging day today, I got several trades, the largest profit was 70+pps, and others around 30pps. I have left sdtill a lot on the table.  
happy trading  
2be

Hi Paulus,  
The 5min Keltner is a good filter to get in and out of the market. I trade cycles which can be observed on different TFs. I have added CCI Woddies set on 34 on 5min, as an additional indicator, and compare it in terms of cycle with the 15min (CCI set on 14), H1( CCI multi set at 5,8,14 and 34) and H4(DiNapoli settings and CCI multi) TFs. I know this is not the way you have originally intended to use this system, but it has been working for me as a trigger filter. The gearing between different TFs is usefull while trading both ways in relation to the trend discerned on a H4 or Daily TF.  
Wishing you many good trades,  
2be

  * [#406](/thread/post/4963314#post4963314 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 10:06am  Sep 18, 2011 9:53am | Edited 10:06am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar194063_3.gif) dmacattack](dmacattack)

  * | Joined Sep 2011  | Status: Trader | [13 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=194063)

hello gonso  
  
I'm looking at using this method and I believe I have found a way to substantially lower the risk involved in these "counter trend" trades. It goes as follows:  
  
I am looking at eurusd 5min tf on the 14th of this month, starting at the 1720 candle. During this trend upward we see several signals to short, none of which would have reached the initial TP level specified by the rules of this system(1720, 1845, and 1955 jump out at me as entry points). Finally at the 2025 is a signal to short where the TP level is reached before the stop.  
  
If you notice during this time PA never touches the bottom of the Keltner channel. The rule should be if you have a losing trade to ignore all signals in the same direction after that loosing trade until PA reaches the bottom(or top for long) of the Keltner channel, giving an indication that the recent trend is over.  
  
A more strict rule could be as follows: After a losing trade, the next trade MUST be the opposite order of the losing one.  
  
Applying these rules in the example above we would have a loser at 1720, then the next trade we would take would be at 2145(since PA touched the bottom band earlier). Applying the more strict rule would put a pass on the 2145 short but would take the 2215 long.  
  
Another thing to possibly look at is the angle the bands make. The angle is high(either + or -) during these trends. One could just pass on all trades until the angle is small, lets say within 15 degrees from 0. Let me know what you think.  
-Dan 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Well , the only real difference is that it is on a renko chart (3 box size ) ..  
  
I have the keltner set to 1.5 , but actually have only been using the stoch (15/3/2 ) for entry and exit .  
  
Put it on a renko chart and see what you think ..  
  
A renko setting of 5 will give fewer but more dependable signals .  
  
As Paulus has said a bollinger band doesn't work as well , as it expands and contracts .

No , it is an indicator , not an EA ..  
  
Go to : My Computer/Drive C/Program Files/MT4/Experts/Indicators.....  
  
Drag & drop in indicators ..  
  
Close and re-open MT4 , and it will be under Insert/Indicators/Custom  
  
Then install it on a 1min chart and then open the offline chart

direction is visible , you should be safe .

  * Jan 30, 2012 7:30am  Jan 30, 2012 7:30am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar167532_2.gif) Kilian19](kilian19)

  * Joined Jan 2011 | Status: Currently in Asia | [839 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=167532)

Hey chappy I used to work with Renko charts a lot and I really liked them.   
It seems like the system you are using is a mechanical system can you please post the exact rules and I will write an EA and release it here.  
Thanks a lot 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#438](/thread/post/5337387#post5337387 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2012 5:48pm  Jan 30, 2012 5:48pm 

  * [ chappy](chappy)

  * | Joined Apr 2011  | Status: Trader | [48 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=175508)

Wow , That would be great if you could do it .  
  
I use the basc rules from Paulus's 1st post .  
  
long signal :  
  
1\. Wait for price to be outside keltner , and stoch below 20 .  
  
2\. Enter as stoch crosses up through 20 .  
  
3\. Exit as price touches opposite keltner . ( You could also hold until stoch  
  
goes up through the 80 and then exit as it comes back down through the   
  
80 , but this may be a bit much for an EA .)  
  
I also set the Keltner to 1.5 ATR  
  
Stoch : 15/3/2  
  
  
Paulus also moves the stop to BE at mid channel , I haven't been doing   
  
that . but might be a good idea for an EA .  
  
Hope this is clear enough ..Let me know if I can help ..  
  
Thanks Again .......

  * Jan 30, 2012 11:06pm  Jan 30, 2012 11:06pm 

  * [ chappy](chappy)

  * | Joined Apr 2011  | Status: Trader | [48 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=175508)

Sorry , I think I confused you ,   
  
when the stoch crosses the 20 ( to go long ) , price has usually also crossed   
  
back into the keltner . The entry signal for me is when the stoch crosses the   
  
20 ,  
  
Paulus does it a little differently with candlesticks by taking the first long bar  
  
and not waiting for the stach to cross ..  
  
btw ,,today is a tough day for the method on the EU , as we are in a trend .  
  
This method works best in a sideways , rangebound day .

  * [ chappy](chappy)

This might be a way to use the method in a trend .  
  
The stoch has failed to retrace from OS to OB ( or vice versa ) so when it   
  
comes back to the 20/80 , it signals a continuation entry ..  
  
( a bit confusing but gets clearer with screen time )  
.........................................................................................  
  
Kilian , I'm not sure how to answer that for coding purposes ..However   
  
for a sell signal ,when the price moves above the keltner ,it tells me   
  
"heads-up"--"get ready " . at that point i am focused on the stoch . and as   
  
it slants down towards the 80 , I will enter just as it crosses ..  
  
Lol ..I guess I am saying that No , I'm not waiting for a bar to close ..  
  
The action of the stoch is my main focus ..Hope that all makes some sense  
  
Having said that , Paulus uses a bar close entry and he may get in before I do .

  * [#449](/thread/post/6322018#post6322018 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 26, 2012 11:07pm  Dec 26, 2012 11:07pm 

  * [ LeW](lew)

  * | Joined Jun 2010  | Status: Trader | [43 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=144266)

Hi!  
  
I have an idea how to tading with success using keltner channel   
  
1/ TP should be 2 times higher than SL (eg. SL = 30% x distance between channels lines, TP = 60% x dist)  
2/ After SL, wait for opposite signal (eg. if sell signal closed by SL, EA wait only for buy signal)  
3/ Every trade with fixed risk (eg. 0,5 - 1 %)  
4/ Open trade some pips above lower line / below higher line (2-3 pips)  
  
Can anyone code the EA using this rules?  
I'll be grateful.  
  
LeW 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#450](/thread/post/6373872#post6373872 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 18, 2013 2:17am  Jan 18, 2013 2:17am 

  * [ LeW](lew)

  * | Joined Jun 2010  | Status: Trader | [43 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=144266)

(The important thing which makes this EA profitable)  
  
5/ Add 1.5 lot multiplier after StopLoss  
1) Start with 0,2% risk  
2) 0,3%  
3) 0,4%  
4) 0,6%  
5) 0,9%  
6) 1,3%  
7) 1,9%  
8) 2,8%  
9) 4,2%  
10) 6,3%  
11) 6,3%  
12) Stop trading and move the EA to recycle bin

  * [#451](/thread/post/6398230#post6398230 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 28, 2013 7:09pm  Jan 28, 2013 7:09pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar59694_4.gif) colombino](colombino)

  * | Joined Jan 2008  | Status: Trader | [155 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=59694)

Well I have manualy bactested this method (the original one, not LeW's modification) and this is not a winning strategy in long run.  
There are days with haevy winning but then come day with like 3W/17L. The truth is, that winning trades are bigger then the losing ones, but it will not help make tis method a winning strategy. In the long run you will got none or really thin edge over the market.  
What I noticed is, that 5,3,2 stoch filter is not good at all, the best is the original 15,3,2 stoch, in combination with diNapoli even better. Using BE at middle white line is not good too.
